        <td id="LC93" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">2 CHIP	recently	engaged	an	independent 3 research	firm	called	Urbanomics	to	examine	and 4 characterize	the	owners	of	rent	stabilized 5 property .         <td id="LC247" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">2 Guidelines	Board	on	its	proposed	rent	increases 3 for	the	approximately	one	million	apartments 4 that	remain	subject	to	the	New	York	City	Rent 5 Stabilization	Law .6 I	am	dismayed	that	the	RGB	is	even 7 considering	rent	increases	of 2	percent	to	4 . 58 percent	for	one - year	lease	renewals	and	49 percent	to	7 . 5	percent	for	two - year	lease 10 renewals	in	light	of	the	current	economic 11 climate	and	the	steady	rent	increases	the	RGB 12 has	approved	in years	past .13 Passing	additional	financial	burdens 14 onto	tenants ,	many	of	whom	are	still	reeling 15 from	prior	increases ,	would	be	an	unfair	and 16 unnecessary	hardship ,	particularly	when	the 17 RGB &#39; s	own	yearly	Income	and	Expense	Studies 18 from	2007	to	2009	have	shown	landlords &#39; net 19 operating	income	has	increased	1 . 9	percent ,	8 . 820 percent	and	9 . 3 percent	respectively .21 As you	know ,	these	are	especially 22 difficult	times	for	New	York &#39; s	working	people .23 In his	Fiscal	Year	2010	Executive 24 Budget	released	on	May	1 ,	2009 ,	Mayor	Bloomberg 25 forecast	that	the	City	will	lose	328 , 000	jobs 2 </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L248" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="248"></td>
        <td id="LC248" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> 2 during	this	recession	and	stated	that	105 , 000 3 jobs	had	already	been	lost	since	August	2008 .4 In his	testimony	last	month	before 5 the	RGB ,	James	Parrot ,	Deputy	Director	and 6 Chief	Economist	of	the	Fiscal	Policy	Institute ,7 noted	that	the	City	unemployment	rate	has	risen 8 to	8 . 2	percent	while	real	median	wages	fell	by 9 3 . 5 percent	from	2001	to	2008 ,	and	the	median 10 household	income	for	renters ,	adjusted	for 11 inflation ,	fell	by	4 . 2	percent	from	2001	to 12	2007 .13 According	to	U . S .	Representative 14 Anthony	Weiner , Federal	census	data	shows	that 15 more	than	a	quarter	of	New	York	City	renters 16 are	spending	fifty	percent	or more	of	their 17 income	on	housing .18 New	York &#39; s	rent	regulated	tenants 19 simply	cannot	afford	another	rent	increase 20 under	these	circumstances .21 The	RGB	has	historically	justified 22 annual	rent	increases	by	citing	its	Price	Index 23 of	Operating	Costs .	This	year &#39; s	Price	Index 24 found	that	operating	costs	for	rent - stabilized 25 buildings	increased	by	4	percent	in	the	past 13 </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L249" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="249"></td>
        <td id="LC249" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">2 year ,	down	from	7 . 8	percent	in	2008 .3 However ,	as	I	noted	in	my	testimony 4 before	you	last	year ,	the	Price	Index	measures 5 changes	in	the	cost	of	items	landlords 6 typically	purchase	to	run	their	buildings ,7 rather	than	actual	expenditures ,	and	it 8 contains	no	information	about	the	incomes 9 landlords	collect .10 As a	result ,	it is	misleading	and	it 11 is	not	an	appropriate	tool	to use	to	justify 12 rent	increases .13 A	more	meaningful	report	is the 14 RGB &#39; s	annual	Income	and	Expense	Study	because 15 it	shows	landlords &#39;	net	operating	income .	The 16 RGB &#39; s	2009	Income	and	Expense	Study	shows	that ,17 even	while	landlords &#39;	operating	costs	increased 18 by	5 . 2	percent	over	the	price	year ,	their 19 rental	income	increased	by	6 . 5	percent	and	net 20 operating	income	increased	9 . 3	percent .21 Last	year ,	the	RGB	ignored	its 22 Income	and	Expense	Study	which	showed 23 landlords &#39;	net	operating	income	had	increased 24 8 . 8 percent ,	and	passed	its	highest	rent 25 increases	in	twenty	years :	4 . 5	percent	for 2 </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L250" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="250"></td>
        <td id="LC250" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">2 one - year	lease	renewals	and	8 . 5	percent	for 3 two - year	lease	renewals .4 This	exposes	the	degree	to which	the 5 system	is	skewed	against	tenants .	Indeed ,	this 6 fundamental	anti - tenant	bias	is	one	of	the 7 reasons	New	York	State	Assemblymember	George 8 Latimer	and	I	have	introduced	and	are	committed 9 to	passing	a	Rent	Board	Reform	bill	that	would 10 revamp	the	method	of	establishing	rent 11 adjustments	- -12 ( Applause . )13 MR . ROMEO	YMALAY :	- -	for 14 rent - regulated	apartments	in New	York	City	and 15 suburban	counties .16 While	we	continue	to	press	for 17 passage	of	this	legislation , it	behooves	the 18 RGB	to	reject	rent	increases	that	serve	only	to 19 enhance	landlord	profits	and	further 20 destabilize	New	York	City &#39; s affordable	housing 21 stock .22 As you	all	are	very	much	aware ,	New 23 York	continues	to be	in	a	housing	crisis	with 24 affordable	housing	stock	rapidly	dwindling	in 25 the	midst	of	the	worst	economic	downturn	since 2 </td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC254" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">4 &quot; Changes	to	the	Rent	Stabilized	Housing	Stock 5 in	New	York	City	in	2008 , &quot;	there	was	a	net 6 decrease	of	8 , 267	rent - stabilized	apartments 7 throughout	the	five	boroughs	last	year , over 8 3000	more	units	than	were	lost	in	2007 .9 The	report	cites	Division	of	Housing 10 and	Community	Renewal	rent	registration	records 11 that	indicate	12 , 800	units	were	deregulated	in 12 2008	because	of the	vacancy	decontrol	law ,	an 13 alarming	increase	- -14 CHAIRMAN	MARKUS :	You	need	to	wrap 15 up .16 MR .         <td id="LC255" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">2 adjustments	based	on	the	relative	cost	of 3 maintaining	and	financing	buildings ,	the 4 available	housing	supply	as defined	by	the 5 vacancy	rate ,	and	the	cost	of living .6 If the	Board	bases	its	decision	on 7 these	standards , and	I	strongly	urge	it to	do 8 so , it	will	impose	a	freeze	on	rents	for	all 9 rent	regulated	apartments	as well	as	for	lofts ,10 hotels ,	rooming	houses ,	single	room	occupancy 11 buildings	and	lodging	houses .12 Given	all	the	facts ,	the	only 13 acceptable	outcome	of	this	Board &#39; s	vote	is	no 14 rent	increases .15 Thank	you	for	your	consideration	of 16 my	remarks .17 CHAIRMAN	MARKUS :	Thank	you .18 ( Applause . )19 CHAIRMAN	MARKUS :	Question .20 MS .
